[[faq]]
q = 'What is the USN helium-oxygen (HeO2) decompression table?'
a = 'Table 12-4 of the U.S. Navy Diving Manual Revision 7 is the Surface-Supplied Helium-Oxygen Decompression Table. It covers depths from 60 to over 380 FSW with a descent rate of 75 FPM and ascent rate of 30 FPM. Decompression uses the bottom helium-oxygen mix at 50 FSW and deeper, switches to 50% O2 at 40 FSW, and uses 100% O2 at 30 and 20 FSW stops.'

[[faq]]
q = 'Why is helium-oxygen (HeO2) used instead of air for deep diving?'
a = 'Helium-oxygen mixtures are used for diving deeper than approximately 150-200 FSW because helium does not cause nitrogen narcosis, allows faster ascent and shorter decompression times compared to air at equivalent depths, and avoids high-pressure nervous syndrome better than air at extreme depths. HeO2 is the standard breathing gas for deep surface-supplied commercial diving operations.'

[[faq]]
q = 'What are the gas switches in USN HeO2 decompression?'
a = 'USN Table 12-4 specifies three gas phases during decompression: (1) Bottom Mix (HeO2) for all stops at 50 FSW and deeper; (2) Switch to 50% O2 at the 40 FSW stop; (3) Switch to 100% O2 at the 30 FSW and 20 FSW stops. These gas switches are mandatory — they accelerate decompression and reduce inert gas loading.'

[[faq]]
q = 'What is the maximum depth covered by USN HeO2 tables?'
a = 'USN Table 12-4 explicitly covers surface-supplied helium-oxygen diving to depths beyond 380 FSW, with exceptional exposure procedures for deep dives. The table provides decompression schedules for standard and exceptional exposure dives, with bottom times at each depth section clearly showing where Commanding Officer authorization is required for exceptional exposures.'

[[faq]]
q = 'What is the MK 16 MOD 1 UBA and how do its tables differ?'
a = 'The MK 16 MOD 1 UBA (Underwater Breathing Apparatus) is a closed-circuit rebreather used by U.S. Navy divers. Its decompression tables differ from open-circuit surface-supplied tables because the rebreather maintains a constant partial pressure of oxygen (PPO2) throughout the dive, which changes the decompression obligation compared to open-circuit breathing. The MK 16 tables specify procedures for different PPO2 setpoints and depth ranges.'

[[faq]]
q = 'How does surface decompression work with HeO2 diving?'
a = 'Surface decompression (SurDO2) with HeO2 involves ascending from the last in-water stop, transferring the diver to a deck recompression chamber, and completing the remaining decompression obligation breathing 100% oxygen under pressure. The "Chamber O2 Periods" column in Table 12-4 specifies the number of 30-minute oxygen breathing periods required in the chamber after surfacing.'
+++

# U.S. Navy Diving Manual — Revision 7 HeO2 and Mixed Gas Dive Tables

**Source:** SS521-AG-PRO-010, U.S. Navy Diving Manual, Revision 7, 01 December 2016
**NAVSEA Reference:** Published by Direction of Commander, Naval Sea Systems Command

> **CRITICAL WARNING:** These tables are transcribed from the official USN Diving Manual Revision 7. **They must be verified against the original publication before operational use.** Transcription errors, however unlikely, could be fatal. Always cross-reference with the official NAVSEA publication.

{{< download-page "Download Tables as PDF" >}}

## About These Tables

These tables apply to helium-oxygen (HeO2) and mixed gas diving using surface-supplied equipment (SSDS) and the MK 16 MOD 1 closed-circuit UBA. HeO2 is the standard breathing gas for deep commercial and naval diving operations where nitrogen narcosis and extended air decompression would be limiting factors.

**Key differences from air tables:**
- No nitrogen narcosis at depth (helium is narcosis-free)
- Faster uptake and elimination kinetics than nitrogen
- Gas switches during decompression (HeO2 → 50% O2 → 100% O2) dramatically shorten decompression time
- Chamber oxygen periods required post-dive
- Commanding Officer authorization required for exceptional exposure bottom times

---

## Table 12-4. Surface-Supplied Helium-Oxygen Decompression Table

**(DESCENT RATE 75 FPM — ASCENT RATE 30 FPM)**

**Gas Switches:**
- **Bottom Mix (HeO2):** All stops at 50 FSW and deeper
- **50% O2:** Stop at 40 FSW
- **100% O2:** Stops at 30 and 20 FSW

**Notes:**
- Stop times (min) include travel time, except first HeO2 stop and first O2 stop
- "Chamber O2 Periods" indicates required post-dive chamber oxygen breathing periods (each period = 30 minutes)
- Bottom times listed after "Exceptional Exposure" line require Commanding Officer's authorization

### 60 FSW

Max O2 = 40.0% | Min O2 = 14.0%

| Bottom Time (min) | Time to 1st Stop (M:S) | 40 ft | 30 ft | 20 ft | Chamber O2 Periods |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 10 | 2:00 | | | 0 | 0 |
| 20 | 2:00 | | | 0 | 0 |
| 30 | 2:00 | | | 0 | 0 |
| 40 | 2:00 | | | 0 | 0 |
| 60 | 0:40 | 10 | 11 | 16 | 1 |
| 80 | 0:40 | 10 | 13 | 22 | 2 |
| 100 | 0:40 | 10 | 16 | 27 | 2 |
| 120 | 0:40 | 10 | 17 | 28 | 2 |

## MK 16 MOD 1 Closed-Circuit UBA Tables (1.3 ata ppO2)

**(DESCENT RATE 60 FPM — ASCENT RATE 30 FPM)**

The following tables apply to the MK 16 MOD 1 closed-circuit underwater breathing apparatus operating at a constant partial pressure of oxygen of 1.3 ata.

---

## Table 15-8. No Decompression Limits and Repetitive Group Designators for 1.3 ata ppO2 N2O2 Dives

**Notes:**
- **–** Diver does not acquire a repetitive group designator during dives to these depths
- **\*** Highest repetitive group that can be achieved at this depth regardless of bottom time
- Depths at 160 FSW and deeper are **Exceptional Exposure** (require CO authorization)

| Depth (fsw) | No-Stop Limit | A | B | C | D | E | F | G | H | I | J | K | L | M | N | O | Z |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|

| 15 | Unlimited | – | – | – | – | – | – | – | – | – | – | – | – | – | – | – | – |
| 20 | Unlimited | 153 | 420 | * | | | | | | | | | | | | | |
| 25 | Unlimited | 51 | 87 | 133 | 196 | 296 | 557 | * | | | | | | | | | |
| 30 | Unlimited | 31 | 50 | 72 | 98 | 128 | 164 | 210 | 273 | 372 | 629 | * | | | | | |

| 40 | Unlimited | 89 | 168 | 318 | * | | | | | | | | | | | | |
| 50 | Unlimited | 27 | 44 | 63 | 84 | 108 | 136 | 169 | 210 | 265 | 344 | 496 | * | | | | |
| 60 | 297 | 16 | 25 | 36 | 46 | 58 | 70 | 83 | 97 | 113 | 130 | 149 | 170 | 194 | 222 | 255 | 297 |
| 70 | 130 | 11 | 18 | 25 | 32 | 39 | 47 | 55 | 64 | 73 | 83 | 93 | 103 | 115 | 127 | 130 | |
| 80 | 70 | 9 | 14 | 19 | 24 | 30 | 36 | 42 | 48 | 54 | 61 | 68 | 70 | | | | |

## Table 15-9. Residual Nitrogen Timetable for 1.3 ata ppO2 N2O2 Dives

This table has two parts:
1. **Surface Interval Credit Table** — Determines new repetitive group after a surface interval
2. **Residual Nitrogen Times** — Minutes of residual nitrogen time for the repetitive dive

##### Part 1: Surface Interval Credit Table

Locate your previous repetitive group designation. Read horizontally to find the column where your surface interval falls. Read down to find your new repetitive group.

**\*** = Dives following surface intervals longer than this are not repetitive dives. Use actual bottom times in the Tables 15-8 and 15-10 to compute decompression for such dives.

All times in h:mm format.

| Previous Group | New Group: Z | O | N | M | L | K | J | I | H | G | F | E | D | C | B | A | Not Rep (>) |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Z** | 0:10–0:52 | 0:53–1:44 | 1:45–2:37 | 2:38–3:29 | 3:30–4:21 | 4:22–5:13 | 5:14–6:06 | 6:07–6:58 | 6:59–7:50 | 7:51–8:42 | 8:43–9:34 | 9:35–10:27 | 10:28–11:19 | 11:20–12:13 | 12:14–13:30 | 13:31–15:50 | 15:50 |
| **O** | | 0:10–0:52 | 0:53–1:44 | 1:45–2:37 | 2:38–3:29 | 3:30–4:21 | 4:22–5:13 | 5:14–6:06 | 6:07–6:58 | 6:59–7:50 | 7:51–8:42 | 8:43–9:34 | 9:35–10:27 | 10:28–11:21 | 11:22–12:37 | 12:38–14:58 | 14:58 |

**–** = Repetitive dives to these depths are equivalent to remaining on the surface. Add the bottom time of the dive to the preceding surface interval. Use the Surface Interval Credit Table (SICT) to determine the repetitive group at the end of the dive.

## MK 16 MOD 1 Closed-Circuit UBA Tables — 1.3 ata ppO2 HeO2

The following tables apply to the MK 16 MOD 1 closed-circuit underwater breathing apparatus operating at a constant partial pressure of oxygen of 1.3 ata, using helium-oxygen (HeO2) as the breathing gas.

## Table 15-12. Residual Helium Timetable for 1.3 ata ppO2 HeO2 Dives

### Part 1: Surface Interval Credit Table (Helium)

Locate the diver's repetitive group designation from his previous dive in the "Previous Group" column.
Read across to find the interval in which the diver's surface interval lies.
The column header shows the new repetitive group designation.

- Minimum surface interval for a repetitive dive is **0:10** (hours:minutes).
- Surface intervals **less than 0:10** are not permitted.
- Intervals beyond the last value marked with **\*** are **not repetitive** -- use actual bottom times with Tables 15-11 and 15-13.

### Part 2: Residual Helium Times (Minutes)

After determining the new repetitive group designation from Part 1, read down the appropriate column to the row matching the repetitive dive depth to find the Residual Helium Time (RHT) in minutes. Add the RHT to the planned bottom time of the repetitive dive to obtain the equivalent single dive time for decompression planning.

### Table Notes

- **--** Repetitive dives to these depths are equivalent to remaining on the surface. Add the bottom time of the dive to the preceding surface interval. Use the Surface Interval Credit Table (SICT) to determine the repetitive group at the end of the dive.
- **\*\*** Residual Helium Time cannot be determined using this table. See paragraph 9-9.1 subparagraph 8 for guidance. Substitute the ** depths in this table for those in the instructions.
- **+** Read vertically down to the 35 or 60 fsw repetitive dive depth to obtain the RHT. Decompress on the 35 or 60 fsw table.

Locate the diver's repetitive group designation from his previous dive in the left column. Read horizontally to the interval in which the diver's surface interval lies. Read vertically downward to the new repetitive group designation.

### Notes

- **--** Repetitive dives to these depths are equivalent to remaining on the surface. Add the bottom time of the dive to the preceding surface interval. Use the Surface Interval Credit Table (SICT) to determine the repetitive group at the end of the dive.

- **\*\*** Residual Nitrogen Time cannot be determined using this table. See paragraph 9-9.1 subparagraph 8 for guidance. Substitute the \*\* depths in this table for those in the instructions.

## Frequently Asked Questions

### Why use helium-oxygen instead of air at depth?

Air causes nitrogen narcosis at depths beyond ~100 FSW (individual variation), which impairs diver judgment and performance. Helium does not cause narcosis, making HeO2 the preferred gas for deep operations. HeO2 also has faster decompression kinetics than air at equivalent depths due to helium's lower solubility.

### What are the gas switch requirements?

USN Table 12-4 mandates specific gas switches during ascent:
1. **Bottom mix (HeO2)** — all bottom time and stops at 50 FSW and deeper
2. **50% O2** — stop at 40 FSW
3. **100% O2** — stops at 30 and 20 FSW

These switches are non-optional and dramatically reduce total decompression time.

### What does "Chamber O2 Periods" mean?

Each chamber O2 period is 30 minutes of 100% oxygen breathing in a deck recompression chamber (DRC) after surfacing. This surface decompression (SurDO2) completes the decompression obligation started in the water. The number of periods required increases with bottom time and depth.
